 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

## Market Study Dimensions

# Dimensions etudes de marché

 | 
Taille de marché | Volume * frequence
Facilité d'achat et de contact (accessibilité) | Personnalité et contexte
Activité par étape du métier | OK
Objections du métier | OK
Concurrence qui leur vende des services | Début
Valeur ajoutée d'une offre théorique | 

## Business Development Persona

# Steps for Business development

Business development Process - Step-by-Step Analysis |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
step | objective | success_criteria | average_duration | key_deliverables | profiles_involved | role_of_medical_literature | specialized_solution_providers | main_known_risks |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 1: Market Research & Opportunity Identification | To proactively identify emerging scientific trends, unmet medical needs, and potential strategic opportunities (e.g., novel drug candidates, platform technologies, companies) that align with the company's strategic priorities. | Comprehensive market landscape reports covering specific therapeutic areas (e.g., immunology, oncology, rare diseases).; Identification of at least 3-5 high-potential therapeutic areas or technology platforms.; Early detection of significant scientific breakthroughs or competitive shifts. | Ongoing (typically 1-3 months for initial deep dives into new areas, then continuous monitoring). | Market landscape analysis reports (including disease burden, current treatments, competitive analysis).; SWOT (Strengths, Weaknesses, Opportunities, Threats) analysis for target therapeutic areas.; Trend reports on scientific innovation and emerging technologies. | New Business Development Manager: Leads the research, synthesizes findings.; Market Research Analysts: Provide data and insights.; Scientific/Medical Affairs: Offer clinical and scientific perspectives on unmet needs and disease areas.; R&D Scientists: Provide insights into cutting-edge research. | Critical for understanding disease epidemiology, current treatment guidelines, clinical trial results of competitors, emerging therapeutic targets, and the scientific rationale behind novel approaches. This includes peer-reviewed journals, clinical trial databases, and scientific conferences. | Market Intelligence Firms: IQVIA, Evaluate Pharma, GlobalData, Clarivate.; Scientific Databases: PubMed, Scopus, Web of Science.; Patent Databases: Derwent Innovation, Google Patents.; Consulting Firms: Specialized healthcare/life sciences consultancies. | Inaccurate Data: Relying on outdated or unverified market information.; Missing Emerging Trends: Failure to identify disruptive innovations early enough.; Misinterpreting Market Signals: Incorrectly assessing the commercial viability or strategic fit of an opportunity. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 2: Target Identification & Prioritization | To translate identified opportunities into specific, actionable targets (e.g., individual companies, specific drug assets, research programs) and to prioritize them based on strategic fit, scientific merit, commercial potential, and feasibility. | A prioritized list of 5-10 potential partners/assets with clear rationale for each.; Initial, high-level financial and strategic fit assessments for top targets.; Internal alignment on target priorities. | 2-4 weeks per identified opportunity (can be iterative). | Detailed target profiles (company overview, asset pipeline, key personnel, intellectual property).; Initial strategic fit analysis (alignment with company portfolio, capabilities, and goals).; Preliminary commercial attractiveness assessment (market size, competitive advantage). | New Business Development Manager: Leads target identification and prioritization.; R&D/Scientific Leads: Evaluate scientific novelty and technical feasibility.; Finance Team: Provide initial financial modeling and valuation input.; Legal Counsel (early stage): Assess intellectual property landscape and potential legal risks. | Essential for a deeper dive into the scientific validity, clinical data (pre-clinical and clinical trial phases), and competitive differentiation of specific target assets. This informs the assessment of their potential to address unmet medical needs. | Biotech/Pharma Databases: BioCentury, Fierce Biotech, Cortellis.; Investment Banks: Provide industry insights and potential target lists.; Specialized Consulting Firms: For competitive intelligence and strategic analysis. | Overlooking Key Competitors: Underestimating the strength or pipeline of rival companies.; Misjudging Asset Potential: Incorrectly assessing the clinical efficacy or market adoption of a target asset.; Internal Misalignment: Lack of consensus among internal stakeholders on which targets to pursue. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 3: Initial Outreach & Relationship Building | To establish initial contact with the prioritized targets, introduce the company's interest, and build rapport to facilitate deeper discussions. | Securing initial non-confidential meetings with key decision-makers at target companies.; Successful presentation of the company's value proposition and strategic interest.; Establishment of a positive and professional relationship. | 1-2 months per target (can vary widely). | Customized outreach strategy and messaging.; Non-confidential presentation decks tailored to the target's interests.; Meeting summaries and follow-up plans.; Executed Confidentiality Agreements (CDAs/NDAs) to enable sharing of more sensitive information. | New Business Development Manager: Primary contact, leads outreach and initial meetings.; Senior Leadership (e.g., Head of BD, CEO): May participate in initial high-level meetings to demonstrate commitment. | Used to demonstrate the NBDM's understanding of the target company's scientific focus, pipeline, and specific assets. It helps frame discussions around shared scientific interests and potential synergies. | Industry Conferences & Events: Bio-Europe, JP Morgan Healthcare Conference, BIO International Convention.; Professional Networking Platforms: LinkedIn.; Executive Search Firms: Can sometimes provide introductions. | Difficulty Securing Meetings: Targets may not be receptive or available.; Lack of Clear Value Proposition: Failure to articulate how the partnership would benefit the target.; Early Miscommunication: Misunderstandings about intentions or capabilities. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 4: Due Diligence (Preliminary & In-depth) | To conduct a thorough and systematic evaluation of all aspects of the opportunity, including scientific, clinical, regulatory, commercial, legal, and financial, to assess risks, opportunities, and overall value. | Comprehensive due diligence report detailing findings, risks, and mitigations.; Validation of scientific claims and clinical data.; Accurate financial projections and valuation.; Identification of all significant deal-breakers or red flags. | 3-6 months (can be significantly longer for complex M&A or late-stage assets). | Access and review of the target's data room.; Expert interviews (internal and external scientific/clinical experts).; Detailed scientific and clinical assessment reports.; Regulatory pathway analysis.; Commercial market assessment and forecast.; Financial models and valuation reports.; Legal review of intellectual property, contracts, and compliance. | New Business Development Manager: Orchestrates the entire due diligence process.; R&D/Clinical Development Teams: Evaluate scientific data, clinical trial design, and results.; Regulatory Affairs: Assess regulatory pathways, risks, and compliance.; Legal Counsel: Review contracts, IP, and legal liabilities.; Finance Team: Conduct financial modeling, valuation, and synergy analysis.; Commercial/Marketing Teams: Assess market potential, competitive landscape, and commercial strategy.; External Consultants: Scientific experts, market access specialists, intellectual property lawyers, financial advisors. | Crucial for validating scientific claims, understanding the context of clinical trial results, assessing the competitive landscape of similar therapies, and identifying potential regulatory hurdles or market barriers based on existing medical knowledge and guidelines. | Contract Research Organizations (CROs): For clinical data review and analysis.; Specialized Consulting Firms: For scientific, clinical, regulatory, market access, and commercial due diligence.; Legal Firms: For comprehensive legal and IP due diligence.; Financial Advisory Firms: For valuation and financial modeling. | Incomplete Data: Target withholding critical information.; Hidden Liabilities: Undiscovered legal, financial, or regulatory issues.; Over-optimistic Projections: Internal bias leading to inflated commercial or clinical expectations.; Regulatory Challenges: Unexpected hurdles in gaining approval or market access. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 5: Deal Structuring & Negotiation | To design a mutually beneficial deal structure that aligns with both parties' strategic and financial objectives, and to negotiate the terms of the agreement. | Agreement on key deal terms (e.g., upfront payments, milestones, royalties, governance).; Successful negotiation of a term sheet that reflects the agreed-upon structure.; Preservation of key strategic interests for the company. | 2-4 months (highly variable depending on complexity and negotiation dynamics). | Detailed financial models supporting various deal structures.; Term sheet outlining the principal terms and conditions.; Negotiation strategy and talking points.; Internal approval memos for deal terms. | New Business Development Manager: Leads negotiations, proposes deal structures.; Legal Counsel: Drafts and reviews legal documents, advises on legal implications.; Finance Team: Provides valuation expertise, models financial impact of different terms.; Senior Leadership: Provides strategic guidance and final approval on key terms. | Provides the underlying context for valuing assets (e.g., market potential based on disease prevalence, competitive differentiation based on clinical data), which directly influences financial terms like milestones and royalties. | Legal Firms: Specializing in pharmaceutical M&A, licensing, and collaboration agreements.; Financial Advisors/Investment Banks: Provide valuation analysis and negotiation support. | Impasse in Negotiations: Inability to reach mutually acceptable terms.; Unfavorable Terms: Agreeing to terms that do not adequately protect the company's interests or provide sufficient return on investment.; Legal Complexities: Intricate legal frameworks requiring extensive negotiation.; Valuation Discrepancies: Significant differences in how each party values the asset. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 6: Contracting & Closing | To finalize all legal agreements, secure necessary internal and external approvals, and officially close the transaction. | Execution of definitive agreements (e.g., License Agreement, Asset Purchase Agreement, Merger Agreement).; Completion of all closing conditions (e.g., regulatory approvals, shareholder votes).; Public announcement of the deal (if applicable). | 1-2 months (after term sheet agreement). | Final definitive agreements.; Closing checklist and documentation.; Communication plan for internal and external stakeholders.; Press releases or public statements. | New Business Development Manager: Oversees the closing process, coordinates internal teams.; Legal Counsel: Finalizes all legal documentation.; Finance Team: Manages financial aspects of closing.; Senior Leadership: Provides final sign-offs.; Communications Team: Manages public announcements. | Less direct at this stage, but ensures that all scientific and clinical aspects previously assessed are accurately reflected in the final legal documentation and public communications. | Legal Firms: Crucial for drafting and finalizing complex legal agreements.; Regulatory Consultants: For securing necessary regulatory approvals. | Last-Minute Disagreements: Issues arising during final contract drafting.; Regulatory Approval Delays: Unexpectedly long or complex approval processes from antitrust or healthcare authorities.; Failure of Closing Conditions: Inability to meet pre-agreed conditions for closing. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 7: Integration & Alliance Management (Post-Deal) | To ensure the smooth and effective integration of the acquired asset or company into the existing organization, or to manage the ongoing collaboration in the case of an alliance, maximizing the value created by the deal. | Successful transition of assets, personnel, and processes.; Achievement of integration milestones and synergy targets.; Effective ongoing collaboration and communication in alliances.; Realization of the strategic and financial objectives of the deal. | Ongoing (can range from 6 months for simple integrations to several years for complex M&A). | Detailed integration plan and roadmap.; Alliance management framework and governance structure.; Regular performance reviews and progress reports.; Problem-solving and conflict resolution within alliances. | New Business Development Manager: Often transitions to an alliance management role or remains involved in overseeing integration.; Project Management Office (PMO): Leads integration efforts.; R&D, Commercial, Manufacturing, HR, IT: Key functional teams involved in integration.; Dedicated Alliance Managers: For long-term partnerships. | Continues to inform R&D strategies for the acquired asset, guides clinical development plans, and shapes the commercial positioning based on evolving medical knowledge and competitive landscape. | Integration Consultants: For complex M&A integrations.; Alliance Management Platforms/Software: To track alliance performance and communication. | Cultural Clashes: Difficulties in merging different organizational cultures.; Integration Challenges: Operational hurdles in combining systems, processes, and teams.; Failure to Meet Post-Deal Milestones: Underperformance of the acquired asset or alliance.; Loss of Key Personnel: Departure of critical talent post-acquisition. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

## Chief Medical Officer Persona

# Steps for Chief Medical Officer

Chief Medical Officer - Step-by-Step Analysis |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
step | objective | success_criteria | average_duration | key_deliverables | profiles_involved | role_of_medical_literature | specialized_solution_providers | main_known_risks |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 1: Medical Strategy & Vision Leadership | To define and lead the overall medical strategy, ensuring alignment with corporate objectives and patient needs across all therapeutic areas. | A clear, actionable medical strategy document approved by the Executive Committee.; Integration of patient insights into medical strategy.; Consistent communication of medical vision across the organization. | Ongoing (Annual strategic planning, continuous refinement). | Medical Strategic Plan.; Patient Journey Maps.; Unmet Medical Needs Assessments.; Executive presentations and communications. | Chief Medical Officer: Leads medical strategy development.; CEO/Executive Committee: Provides corporate direction and approval.; R&D Heads: Aligns on clinical development strategy.; Commercial/Marketing Heads: Integrates medical insights into commercial strategy.; Patient Advocacy Leads: Provides patient perspectives. | Crucial for understanding disease epidemiology, evolving treatment paradigms, unmet medical needs, and the competitive landscape to inform strategic medical direction. | Management Consulting Firms: McKinsey, BCG, Bain (for strategic frameworks).; Patient Advocacy Organizations.; Market Intelligence Firms: IQVIA, Evaluate Pharma.; Scientific Advisory Boards (SABs). | Inaccurate Data: Relying on outdated or unverified market information.; Missing Emerging Trends: Failure to identify disruptive innovations early enough.; Misinterpreting Market Signals: Incorrectly assessing the commercial viability or strategic fit of an opportunity. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 2: Clinical Development Oversight & Governance | To provide strategic and medical oversight for all clinical development programs (Phases I-IV), ensuring scientific rigor, ethical conduct, and patient safety. | Successful progression of clinical assets through all phases.; Robust clinical trial designs and execution.; Strong patient safety monitoring and reporting.; Achievement of clinical endpoints and regulatory milestones. | Ongoing (Throughout the entire drug development lifecycle). | Clinical Development Plans.; Investigator Brochures (IBs).; Clinical Study Protocols.; Clinical Study Reports (CSRs).; Safety Management Plans.; Data Monitoring Committee (DMC) reports. | Chief Medical Officer: Provides ultimate medical oversight for clinical programs.; Clinical Development Leads (MDs): Design and execute trials.; Biostatisticians: Ensure statistical rigor.; Clinical Operations: Manages trial conduct.; Pharmacovigilance: Monitors and reports adverse events.; Regulatory Affairs: Ensures compliance with clinical regulations.; Ethics Committees/IRBs: Provide ethical review. | Absolutely critical for designing scientifically sound clinical trials, interpreting clinical data, ensuring patient safety, and understanding the evolving standard of care and competitor clinical data. | CROs for clinical trial management and execution.; Specialized Clinical Consulting Firms.; Data Safety Monitoring Boards (DSMBs).; Medical Writing Agencies.; Central Labs for sample analysis. | Overlooking Key Competitors: Underestimating the strength or pipeline of rival companies.; Misjudging Asset Potential: Incorrectly assessing the clinical efficacy or market adoption of a target asset.; Internal Misalignment: Lack of consensus among internal stakeholders on which targets to pursue. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 3: Regulatory Affairs & Health Authority Interactions | To lead interactions with global health authorities, providing medical expertise to support regulatory submissions, approvals, and post-marketing commitments. | Timely and successful regulatory submissions (INDs, NDAs/BLAs, MAAs).; Positive relationships and effective communication with health authorities.; Successful drug approvals.; Compliance with all regulatory requirements and post-marketing commitments. | Ongoing (Intensive during submission and review periods). | Regulatory Strategy Plans.; Briefing Documents for health authority meetings.; Responses to Health Authority Queries.; Post-Marketing Commitment Plans.; Labeling and Prescribing Information. | Chief Medical Officer: Key medical voice in regulatory interactions.; Regulatory Affairs Leads: Manage submission process.; Clinical Development: Provides clinical data.; Pre-clinical Development: Provides pre-clinical data.; Legal Counsel: Advises on regulatory law and compliance. | Essential for understanding regulatory guidelines, presenting clinical data effectively, addressing safety concerns, and ensuring that product labeling accurately reflects the medical evidence. | Regulatory Consulting Firms.; Legal Firms specializing in pharmaceutical regulatory affairs.; Medical Writing Agencies for regulatory documents. | Difficulty Securing Meetings: Targets may not be receptive or available.; Lack of Clear Value Proposition: Failure to articulate how the partnership would benefit the target.; Early Miscommunication: Misunderstandings about intentions or capabilities. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 4: Medical Affairs Leadership & Scientific Exchange | To build and lead a robust Medical Affairs function, driving scientific exchange with the medical community, generating real-world evidence, and ensuring appropriate medical education. | Strong relationships with Key Opinion Leaders (KOLs) and medical societies.; High-quality medical publications and presentations.; Robust Real-World Evidence (RWE) generation.; Effective medical education programs for HCPs. | Ongoing. | Medical Affairs Strategic Plan.; Publication Plans.; RWE Study Protocols.; Medical Education Materials.; KOL Engagement Plans.; Advisory Board Meeting Summaries. | Chief Medical Officer: Oversees Medical Affairs strategy and execution.; Medical Affairs Leads (MSLs, Medical Directors): Engage with KOLs, manage publications.; Health Economics and Outcomes Research (HEOR) Teams: Design RWE studies.; Publications Teams: Manage scientific communications.; Compliance/Legal: Ensures ethical and compliant medical activities. | Fundamental for staying abreast of the latest research, informing scientific exchange, guiding RWE studies, and ensuring medical accuracy in all communications to healthcare professionals. | Medical Communications Agencies.; HEOR Consulting Firms.; Publication Management Software.; KOL Management Platforms.; Scientific Conference Organizers. | Incomplete Data: Target withholding critical information.; Hidden Liabilities: Undiscovered legal, financial, or regulatory issues.; Over-optimistic Projections: Internal bias leading to inflated commercial or clinical expectations.; Regulatory Challenges: Unexpected hurdles in gaining approval or market access. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 5: Patient Safety & Pharmacovigilance Oversight | To ensure robust pharmacovigilance systems are in place for all products, safeguarding patient safety throughout the lifecycle and ensuring compliance with global reporting requirements. | Comprehensive safety monitoring plans for all products.; Timely and accurate reporting of adverse events.; Effective risk management and mitigation strategies.; Compliance with global pharmacovigilance regulations. | Ongoing. | Pharmacovigilance Master File.; Safety Data Exchange Agreements.; Risk Management Plans (RMPs).; Periodic Safety Update Reports (PSURs).; Signal Detection and Management Processes. | Chief Medical Officer: Ultimate responsibility for patient safety.; Head of Pharmacovigilance: Manages daily PV operations.; Clinical Development: Provides safety data from trials.; Regulatory Affairs: Manages safety reporting to agencies.; Quality Assurance: Ensures PV system compliance.; Data Scientists: For safety signal detection. | Critical for identifying, assessing, and communicating potential safety risks associated with drugs, reviewing published safety data, and understanding the epidemiology of adverse events. | Pharmacovigilance Consulting Firms.; Safety Database Providers (e.g., Argus, ArisG).; Drug Safety and Risk Management Software. | Impasse in Negotiations: Inability to reach mutually acceptable terms.; Unfavorable Terms: Agreeing to terms that do not adequately protect the company's interests or provide sufficient return on investment.; Legal Complexities: Intricate legal frameworks requiring extensive negotiation.; Valuation Discrepancies: Significant differences in how each party values the asset. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 6: Ethical Conduct & Compliance | To ensure all medical and clinical activities adhere to the highest ethical standards, industry codes, and regulatory requirements. | Zero major compliance breaches.; Robust internal policies and procedures for ethical conduct.; Regular compliance training for medical teams.; Strong culture of integrity and transparency. | Ongoing. | Code of Conduct and Ethics Policies.; Compliance Training Programs.; Internal Audit Reports.; Standard Operating Procedures (SOPs) for medical activities.; Disclosure of Conflicts of Interest. | Chief Medical Officer: Sets the ethical tone and ensures compliance.; Compliance Officer: Develops and enforces compliance programs.; Legal Counsel: Advises on legal and ethical frameworks.; Internal Audit: Conducts compliance audits.; Human Resources: Manages training and disciplinary actions. | Informs ethical decision-making, ensures adherence to guidelines for patient consent, data privacy, and responsible research practices as outlined in medical and ethical literature. | Ethics Consulting Firms.; Compliance Training Providers.; Legal Firms specializing in healthcare compliance. | Last-Minute Disagreements: Issues arising during final contract drafting.; Regulatory Approval Delays: Unexpectedly long or complex approval processes from antitrust or healthcare authorities.; Failure of Closing Conditions: Inability to meet pre-agreed conditions for closing. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 7: Talent Management & Medical Leadership Development | To recruit, mentor, and develop top medical talent, building a strong, diverse, and high-performing medical organization. | High retention and engagement of medical talent.; Successful succession planning for key medical roles.; Development of future medical leaders.; A diverse and inclusive medical team. | Ongoing. | Medical Talent Acquisition Strategy.; Individual Development Plans (IDPs).; Mentorship Programs.; Leadership Development Programs.; Performance Review Systems.; Diversity & Inclusion Initiatives. | Chief Medical Officer: Leads medical talent strategy, mentors senior staff.; Human Resources: Supports recruitment, development, and retention.; Medical Directors/Managers: Manage and mentor their teams.; Learning & Development Specialists: Design and deliver training programs. | Less direct, but staying current with medical literature is essential for the CMO to guide the professional development of their team, identify emerging areas of medical expertise, and foster a culture of continuous learning. |  | Cultural Clashes: Difficulties in merging different organizational cultures.; Integration Challenges: Operational hurdles in combining systems, processes, and teams.; Failure to Meet Post-Deal Milestones: Underperformance of the acquired asset or alliance.; Loss of Key Personnel: Departure of critical talent post-acquisition. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 8: Cross-Functional & External Collaboration | To foster strong collaborative relationships across internal functions (R&D, Commercial, Legal, etc.) and with external partners (academic, industry, patient groups) to drive shared objectives. | Effective cross-functional project teams.; Productive external partnerships and alliances.; Seamless information flow and decision-making.; Achievement of shared objectives with internal and external stakeholders. | Ongoing. | Cross-Functional Governance Models.; Alliance Management Frameworks.; Joint Steering Committee Charters.; Communication Protocols.; Partnership Performance Reviews. | Chief Medical Officer: Drives cross-functional and external collaboration.; Functional Heads (R&D, Commercial, Legal, BD): Key internal partners.; External Partners (Academics, Biotech CEOs, KOLs): Key external collaborators.; Alliance Managers: Manage specific partnerships. | Informs the strategic rationale for collaborations, helps identify partners with complementary scientific expertise, and supports the medical aspects of joint research or development programs based on published evidence. | Alliance Management Consulting Firms.; Collaboration Platforms/Software.; Industry Associations and Forums. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

## Global Head of Talent Acquisition Persona

# Steps for GLOBAL HEAD OF TA and

GLOBAL HEAD OF TA and/or PORTFOLIO - Step-by-Step Analysis |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
step | objective | success_criteria | average_duration | key_deliverables | profiles_involved | role_of_medical_literature | specialized_solution_providers | main_known_risks |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 1: Strategic Vision & Direction Setting | To establish and articulate a compelling long-term vision and strategic priorities for the assigned therapeutic area or entire portfolio, aligning with overall corporate goals. | A clear, actionable therapeutic area/portfolio strategy document approved by the Executive Committee.; Consistent communication of the vision across relevant functions.; Strategic alignment demonstrated in pipeline decisions and resource allocation. | Ongoing (Annual strategic planning cycle, with continuous refinement). | Therapeutic Area/Portfolio Strategic Plan.; Long-range forecasts (scientific, clinical, commercial).; Strategic imperatives and key performance indicators (KPIs).; Executive presentations and communications. | Global Head of TA/Portfolio: Leads strategy development.; CEO/Executive Committee: Provides ultimate approval and corporate direction.; R&D Heads (Discovery, Clinical, Regulatory): Provide scientific and development input.; Commercial/Marketing Heads: Provide market insights and commercial strategy.; Finance Head: Ensures financial viability and resource planning. | Crucial for identifying future trends, understanding unmet medical needs, assessing competitive landscapes, and evaluating the scientific feasibility of new therapeutic approaches or technologies. | Management Consulting Firms: McKinsey, BCG, Bain (for strategic frameworks).; Market Intelligence Firms: IQVIA, Evaluate Pharma, GlobalData.; Scientific Advisory Boards (SABs).; Foresight and Trend Analysis Consultancies. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 2: Portfolio Optimization & Resource Allocation | To continuously evaluate, prioritize, and optimize the drug pipeline within the therapeutic area/portfolio, ensuring efficient allocation of resources to maximize value and manage risk. | A balanced portfolio with clear progression/gating decisions.; Optimal resource allocation across projects.; High-value projects accelerated, low-value projects deprioritized.; Achievement of portfolio milestones and value inflection points. | Ongoing (Quarterly/bi-annual portfolio reviews). | Integrated Portfolio Dashboard.; Resource Allocation Models.; Go/No-Go Decision Frameworks.; Portfolio Risk Assessments.; Investment proposals for key projects. | Global Head of TA/Portfolio: Drives portfolio decisions and resource allocation.; R&D Project Leads: Provide project status and data.; Finance: Manages budget and investment analysis.; Business Development: Informs on external opportunities.; Regulatory Affairs: Advises on regulatory feasibility and risk. | Essential for assessing the scientific and clinical potential of assets, understanding competitive differentiation, evaluating clinical trial results, and identifying opportunities for label expansion or new indications. | Portfolio Management Software (e.g., Planisware, Sciforma).; Valuation & Financial Modeling Software.; Specialized Analytics Firms for portfolio optimization.; Decision Science Consultants. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 3: Global Development & Commercialization Oversight | To provide strategic oversight for the global development programs within the therapeutic area/portfolio, ensuring successful execution from early research to commercial launch and life cycle management. | Successful progression of assets through clinical phases.; Achievement of regulatory approvals and market access.; Strong commercial performance post-launch.; Effective life cycle management strategies for approved products. | Ongoing (Throughout the entire drug development lifecycle). | Global Development Plans.; Integrated Commercialization Strategies.; Regulatory Submission Roadmaps.; Launch Readiness Plans.; Life Cycle Management Plans. | Global Head of TA/Portfolio: Provides strategic direction and oversight.; Global Project Teams (Cross-functional): Execute development plans.; Clinical Development Leads: Oversee trial design and execution.; Regulatory Leads: Manage health authority interactions.; Commercial Leads: Develop market access and launch strategies.; Manufacturing/Supply Chain: Ensures product availability. | Absolutely critical for understanding disease progression, patient populations, standard of care, clinical trial design, competitor data, and post-marketing surveillance. Guides clinical strategy, regulatory submissions, and commercial messaging. | CROs for global clinical trials.; Global Regulatory Consulting Firms.; Market Access & Reimbursement Consultancies.; Commercial Strategy Firms.; Real-World Evidence (RWE) Platforms. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 4: External Innovation & Business Development Integration | To identify, evaluate, and integrate external innovation opportunities (e.g., licensing, M&A, strategic alliances) that complement and strengthen the therapeutic area/portfolio. | Successful completion of strategic external deals (licensing, M&A).; Seamless integration of new assets/companies into the portfolio.; Value realization from external partnerships.; A robust pipeline of potential external opportunities. | Ongoing (Continuous scouting and deal execution). | External Innovation Strategy.; Due Diligence Reports for potential targets.; Integration Plans for acquired assets/companies.; Alliance Management Frameworks.; Term Sheets and Definitive Agreements. | Global Head of TA/Portfolio: Drives external innovation strategy, approves deals.; Business Development: Identifies and negotiates deals.; R&D Scientists/Leads: Conduct scientific due diligence.; Legal Counsel: Manages legal aspects of deals.; Finance: Performs valuation and financial modeling.; Integration Teams: Manage post-deal integration. | Crucial for assessing the scientific validity, novelty, and clinical potential of external assets, understanding their competitive landscape, and identifying strategic fit with existing portfolio. | Investment Banks.; Biotech/Pharma Partnering Platforms (e.g., BioCentury, Fierce Biotech).; Specialized Due Diligence Consultancies.; Venture Capital Firms (for scouting).; Academic Technology Transfer Offices. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 5: Talent Leadership & Organizational Development | To build, mentor, and lead high-performing global teams within the therapeutic area/portfolio, fostering a culture of scientific excellence, collaboration, and accountability. | High employee engagement and retention rates.; Successful development and promotion of talent.; Effective cross-functional and cross-geographical collaboration.; A strong talent pipeline for key leadership roles. | Ongoing. | Organizational Structure Plans.; Talent Development Programs.; Performance Management Frameworks.; Succession Plans.; Employee Engagement Survey Results. | Global Head of TA/Portfolio: Direct leader, mentor, and talent champion.; Direct Reports (e.g., TA Leads, Functional Heads): Manage their teams.; Human Resources: Supports talent acquisition, development, and retention.; Learning & Development Specialists: Design and deliver training programs. | Less direct; however, a strong understanding of medical literature helps the Global Head guide scientific discussions, identify emerging skill needs in the field, and inspire the team with a vision rooted in scientific advancement and patient impact. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 6: Stakeholder Engagement & Communication | To effectively engage and communicate with a wide range of internal and external stakeholders, including senior leadership, investors, regulatory bodies, key opinion leaders (KOLs), and patient advocacy groups. | Positive relationships with key stakeholders.; Clear and consistent communication of TA/portfolio progress and challenges.; Successful management of stakeholder expectations.; Strong reputation for scientific leadership and patient focus. | Ongoing. | Stakeholder Engagement Plans.; Communication Strategies (internal/external).; KOL Advisory Board Meeting Minutes.; Investor Presentations.; Public Statements/Press Releases. | Global Head of TA/Portfolio: Primary spokesperson and relationship manager.; Investor Relations: Manages investor communications.; Public Relations/Corporate Communications: Manages external messaging.; Medical Affairs: Engages with KOLs and patient groups.; Regulatory Affairs: Manages agency interactions.; Legal Counsel: Ensures compliance in communications. | Essential for engaging with KOLs, patient groups, and regulatory bodies, as it provides the basis for scientific discussions, clinical insights, and understanding patient needs and regulatory expectations. | Public Relations Firms.; Investor Relations Firms.; Medical Communications Agencies.; Patient Advocacy Organizations.; Conference Organizers. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 7: Risk Management & Contingency Planning | To proactively identify, assess, and mitigate strategic, scientific, clinical, regulatory, and commercial risks across the therapeutic area/portfolio, developing robust contingency plans. | Comprehensive risk registers and mitigation plans.; Timely identification of emerging risks.; Effective implementation of contingency plans when needed.; Minimal negative impact from unforeseen challenges. | Ongoing (Regular risk reviews and updates). | Risk Management Framework.; Portfolio Risk Register.; Contingency Plans for critical projects.; Scenario Planning Reports.; Crisis Communication Plans. | Global Head of TA/Portfolio: Oversees risk management strategy.; Project Leads: Identify and manage project-level risks.; Regulatory Affairs: Assesses regulatory risks.; Clinical Development: Assesses clinical risks.; Finance: Assesses financial risks.; Legal Counsel: Assesses legal and compliance risks.; Quality Assurance: Assesses quality risks. | Crucial for understanding potential safety signals, clinical trial failures, regulatory hurdles, or competitive threats based on published data and industry trends. Helps inform proactive risk mitigation strategies. | Risk Management Consulting Firms.; Specialized Legal Counsel for risk assessment.; Data Analytics and Predictive Modeling Tools for risk forecasting. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

## Market Access Persona

# Steps for Market access

 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Pharmaceutical Market Access Process - Step-by-Step Analysis |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step | Objective | Success Criteria | Average Duration | Key Deliverables | Profiles Involved | Role of Medical Literature | Specialized Solution Providers | Main Known Risks |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
1. Market Assessment & Strategy | Define target markets, payer landscape analysis, and develop market access strategy | Clear market prioritization, comprehensive payer mapping, approved strategy document | 3-6 months | Market access strategy document, payer landscape report, pricing corridor analysis | Market Access Directors, Health Economics specialists, Market Research analysts | Epidemiological data, disease burden studies, treatment pathway analysis | IQVIA, Ipsos Healthcare, GlobalData, Evaluate Pharma | Market misunderstanding, competitor intelligence gaps, regulatory changes |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
2. Health Economics & Outcomes Research (HEOR) | Generate evidence on cost-effectiveness, budget impact, and clinical outcomes | Robust economic models, peer-reviewed publications, real-world evidence generation | 12-18 months | Budget impact models, cost-effectiveness analyses, HEOR dossiers, RWE studies | Health Economists, Biostatisticians, Medical Affairs, HEOR specialists | Comparative effectiveness data, safety profiles, clinical trial results, systematic literature reviews | Evidera, Analysis Group, ICON, RTI Health Solutions, OPEN Health | Weak evidence base, model validation issues, data quality concerns, regulatory rejection |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
3. Value Proposition Development | Create compelling value messages tailored to different stakeholders | Stakeholder-specific value propositions, clear differentiation vs. competitors | 2-4 months | Value proposition toolkit, economic value messages, clinical value dossiers | Medical Affairs, Marketing, Health Economics, Market Access managers | Clinical efficacy data, safety evidence, quality of life studies, treatment guidelines | ZS Associates, Simon-Kucher & Partners, Precision AQ, Trinity Life Sciences | Weak differentiation, unconvincing value story, stakeholder misalignment |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
4. Pricing Strategy & Negotiation Preparation | Establish optimal pricing strategy and prepare for payer negotiations | Pricing recommendations approved, negotiation materials ready, stakeholder buy-in | 3-6 months | Pricing strategy document, negotiation playbooks, competitive benchmarking, budget impact tools | Pricing strategists, Market Access Directors, Commercial leadership, Legal team | Comparative clinical data, health economic evidence, treatment cost analyses | Simon-Kucher & Partners, McKinsey, BCG, Deloitte, PwC Strategy& | Pricing too high/low, payer rejection, competitive pressure, regulatory price controls |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
5. Regulatory Health Technology Assessment (HTA) Submissions | Submit comprehensive dossiers to HTA bodies for evaluation | Successful submissions, positive preliminary assessments, stakeholder engagement | 6-12 months | HTA dossiers, clinical evidence packages, economic submissions, response documents | Regulatory Affairs, Medical Writing, HEOR specialists, Market Access | Clinical trial data, indirect treatment comparisons, systematic reviews, real-world evidence | Parexel, IQVIA, Syneos Health, PharmaLex, CARTO | Submission delays, negative assessments, insufficient evidence, regulatory changes |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
6. Payer Engagement & Negotiations | Secure favorable coverage decisions and reimbursement terms | Positive coverage decisions, acceptable pricing agreements, market access secured | 6-18 months | Payer presentations, reimbursement agreements, managed care contracts, access programs | Market Access Directors, Payer Relations specialists, Commercial teams, Legal | Supporting clinical evidence, economic data, real-world outcomes, treatment guidelines | Access Hope, Maple Health Group, ADVI, The Dedham Group | Coverage restrictions, unfavorable terms, delayed decisions, political pressures |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
7. Market Access Implementation | Execute launch strategy and ensure patient access to treatment | Successful product launch, patient access metrics achieved, revenue targets met | 3-12 months | Launch plans, access programs, patient support services, performance dashboards | Commercial teams, Patient Access specialists, Medical Liaisons, Marketing | Ongoing safety data, real-world effectiveness studies, treatment outcome reports | McKesson, AmerisourceBergen, Cardinal Health, Eversana, IQVIA Commercial | Access barriers, distribution issues, patient affordability, competitive responses |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
8. Post-Launch Monitoring & Optimization | Monitor market performance and optimize access strategies continuously | Sustained market access, performance KPIs met, continuous improvement achieved | Ongoing | Performance reports, access optimization plans, stakeholder feedback, competitive intelligence | Market Access analysts, Commercial Intelligence, Medical Affairs, Account managers | Real-world evidence updates, safety surveillance data, comparative effectiveness studies, treatment patterns | Symphony Health, IQVIA Real World Solutions, Veracyte, Flatiron Health | Market access erosion, competitive threats, safety concerns, policy changes |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

## Medical Affairs Persona

# Steps for Medical affairs

 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Pharmaceutical Medical Affairs Process - Step-by-Step Analysis |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step | Objective | Success Criteria | Average Duration | Key Deliverables | Profiles Involved | Role of Medical Literature | Specialized Solution Providers | Main Known Risks |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
1. Medical Strategy Development | Define medical evidence strategy aligned with clinical development and commercial goals | Approved medical strategy, evidence generation plan, stakeholder alignment achieved | 3-6 months | Medical affairs strategy, evidence generation plan, publication strategy, KOL engagement plan | Medical Directors, Medical Science Directors, Medical Strategy leads | Disease area guidelines, treatment algorithms, unmet medical needs analysis, competitive landscape review | Trinity Life Sciences, Precision AQ, OPEN Health, Real Chemistry, Ashfield Healthcare | Misaligned strategy, insufficient evidence planning, competitive disadvantage, stakeholder disconnect |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
2. Key Opinion Leader (KOL) Identification & Engagement | Build relationships with thought leaders and establish advisory networks | Strong KOL network established, advisory boards formed, thought leader partnerships secured | 6-12 months | KOL database, advisory board rosters, speaker bureau, collaboration agreements, engagement tracking | Medical Science Liaisons (MSLs), KOL Management specialists, Medical Directors | Expert publications, congress presentations, clinical practice patterns, thought leadership content | Fishawack Health, Real Chemistry, IQVIA Medical Affairs, Trinity Life Sciences, KOL Networks | Compliance violations, conflict of interest issues, poor KOL selection, relationship management failures |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
3. Medical Information & Scientific Communication | Provide accurate, balanced medical information to healthcare professionals and respond to inquiries | Timely response to medical inquiries, comprehensive medical information database, HCP satisfaction | Ongoing | Medical information responses, scientific monographs, FAQ databases, medical communication materials | Medical Information specialists, Medical Writers, Scientific Communication managers | Clinical trial data, safety literature, product monographs, therapeutic area knowledge base | Parexel Medical Communications, IQVIA Medical Information, Trinity Life Sciences, Complete HealthVizion | Inaccurate information, delayed responses, compliance breaches, off-label promotion risks |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
4. Medical Education & Training | Develop and deliver educational programs for healthcare professionals and internal teams | High-quality educational programs delivered, positive feedback scores, knowledge transfer achieved | 3-12 months | Educational curricula, training materials, webinars, congress symposia, certification programs | Medical Education specialists, Medical Directors, MSLs, External faculty | Evidence-based medicine, clinical guidelines, best practices, educational needs assessments | Real Chemistry, Trinity Life Sciences, Ashfield Healthcare, Complete HealthVizion, Medical Learning Hub | Poor content quality, low engagement, compliance issues, ineffective knowledge transfer |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
5. Publication Planning & Execution | Generate peer-reviewed publications to support medical evidence and thought leadership | Publications accepted in target journals, citation impact achieved, thought leadership established | 12-24 months | Publication plans, manuscripts, congress abstracts, poster presentations, journal supplements | Medical Writers, Publication managers, Medical Directors, External authors | Clinical study results, real-world evidence, systematic reviews, meta-analyses, editorial guidelines | Parexel Medical Communications, Trinity Life Sciences, Real Chemistry, OPEN Health, Fishawack Health | Publication delays, journal rejections, authorship disputes, compliance violations, ghost-writing allegations |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
6. Real-World Evidence Generation | Generate post-market evidence on effectiveness, safety, and health outcomes in clinical practice | RWE studies completed, meaningful insights generated, stakeholder value demonstrated | 12-36 months | RWE study protocols, observational studies, registry analyses, health outcomes research, RWE publications | Real-World Evidence specialists, Medical Epidemiologists, Health Outcomes researchers, Biostatisticians | Epidemiological methods, outcomes research, health technology assessment, comparative effectiveness literature | IQVIA Real World Solutions, Veracyte, Analysis Group, HEOR specialists, ConcertAI | Data quality issues, study design flaws, regulatory challenges, delayed insights, limited generalizability |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
7. Medical Science Liaison Activities | Provide field-based medical support and gather insights from healthcare professionals | Strong HCP relationships, valuable insights collected, medical objectives achieved | Ongoing | Field medical plans, insight reports, congress coverage, investigator meetings, medical support | Medical Science Liaisons, Regional Medical Directors, Medical Affairs Field managers | Current clinical evidence, emerging research, treatment guidelines, clinical practice insights | Ashfield Healthcare, IQVIA Medical Affairs, Trinity Life Sciences, Syneos Health Medical Affairs | Compliance violations, insufficient insights, poor HCP relationships, off-label discussions |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
8. Safety & Risk Management Support | Support pharmacovigilance activities and provide medical oversight of safety signals | Robust safety monitoring, appropriate risk communication, medical input to safety decisions | Ongoing | Safety assessments, risk evaluation reports, medical reviews, safety communications, REMS support | Medical Safety physicians, Medical Directors, Pharmacovigilance specialists | Safety literature, adverse event reports, risk-benefit analyses, clinical safety data | IQVIA Safety, Parexel Safety, Syneos Health Safety, PharmaLex Safety, Amplity Health | Missed safety signals, inadequate risk assessment, poor risk communication, regulatory sanctions |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
9. Medical Affairs Analytics & Insights | Generate actionable insights from medical data and support evidence-based decision making | Data-driven insights delivered, improved decision making, medical objectives achieved | Ongoing | Analytics dashboards, insight reports, competitive intelligence, performance metrics, predictive models | Medical Affairs Analytics specialists, Data Scientists, Medical Information analysts | Competitive publications, clinical trial databases, real-world data sources, medical literature surveillance | IQVIA Medical Affairs Analytics, Veracyte, Symphony Health, Komodo Health, Medical Intelligence | Poor data quality, insufficient insights, delayed reporting, limited actionability, privacy concerns |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

## Project Leader (R&D) Persona

# Steps for Project leader (R&D)

Project Leader (R&D) - Step-by-Step Analysis |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
step | objective | success_criteria | average_duration | key_deliverables | profiles_involved | role_of_medical_literature | specialized_solution_providers | main_known_risks |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 1: Project Initiation & Planning | To define the project scope, objectives, deliverables, and timelines in alignment with R&D strategy and corporate goals. | A comprehensive Project Plan approved by stakeholders.; Clearly defined project scope and objectives.; Realistic timelines and resource estimates.; Identified key milestones and decision points. | 2-4 weeks (for initial planning phase). | Project Charter.; Detailed Project Plan (including scope, objectives, timelines, resources, budget).; Stakeholder Register.; Risk Identification Log (initial). | Project Leader: Leads planning, drafts documents.; R&D Scientists/Team Members: Provide technical input.; Functional Heads (e.g., Discovery, Clinical, Regulatory): Provide resource and strategic input.; Finance: Reviews budget.; Quality Assurance: Advises on quality standards. | Essential for understanding the scientific background of the project, potential challenges, and existing research that may inform experimental design and timelines. | Project Management Software (e.g., Microsoft Project, Asana).; Internal R&D Strategy Documents.; Scientific Databases for background research. | Unclear or shifting scope.; Unrealistic timelines or resource allocation.; Lack of stakeholder alignment.; Incomplete initial risk identification. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 2: Cross-Functional Team Leadership & Coordination | To lead and motivate a multidisciplinary R&D project team, fostering collaboration and ensuring effective communication to achieve project goals. | A cohesive and high-performing project team.; Regular and effective team meetings.; Clear roles and responsibilities for team members.; Timely resolution of inter-team conflicts. | Ongoing throughout project lifecycle. | Team Meeting Agendas and Minutes.; Action Item Trackers.; Communication Plan.; Performance Feedback (informal/formal). | Project Leader: Leads the team, facilitates communication.; R&D Scientists/Team Members: Execute tasks, contribute expertise.; Functional Managers: Provide resources and support for their team members.; HR: Supports team dynamics and conflict resolution. | Less direct, but the Project Leader's understanding of medical literature helps them guide scientific discussions, understand the context of team members' specialized work, and foster a shared scientific vision. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 3: Scientific & Technical Oversight | To provide scientific and technical guidance to the project team, ensuring the integrity, quality, and innovation of the research and development activities. | Sound scientific rationale and experimental design.; High-quality and reproducible data generation.; Effective troubleshooting of scientific challenges.; Adherence to scientific best practices. | Ongoing throughout project lifecycle. | Experimental Design Protocols.; Data Analysis Reports.; Scientific Presentations (internal).; Problem-Solving Logs.; Technical Reports. | Project Leader: Provides scientific direction, reviews data.; R&D Scientists (e.g., Biologists, Chemists, Pharmacologists): Conduct experiments, analyze data.; Senior Scientists/SMEs: Provide specialized technical expertise. | Fundamental for guiding experimental design, interpreting results, troubleshooting scientific challenges, and ensuring the project remains scientifically sound and innovative. Regular review of peer-reviewed journals is critical. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 4: Budget & Resource Management | To manage the project budget and allocate resources effectively, ensuring the project stays within financial constraints and has the necessary personnel and equipment. | Project completed within budget.; Optimal utilization of human and material resources.; Timely procurement of necessary equipment/reagents.; Accurate financial forecasting and reporting. | Ongoing throughout project lifecycle (monthly/quarterly reviews). | Project Budget Tracker.; Resource Allocation Plans.; Procurement Requests.; Financial Variance Reports.; Vendor Contracts. | Project Leader: Manages budget, allocates resources.; Finance Business Partner: Provides financial guidance, tracks spending.; Procurement: Manages vendor relationships and purchasing.; Functional Managers: Allocate personnel to the project. | Less direct, but understanding the cost implications of various research methodologies or specialized equipment (often detailed in scientific literature or vendor information) can inform budget decisions. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 5: Risk Management & Mitigation | To proactively identify, assess, and mitigate potential risks (scientific, technical, operational, regulatory) that could impact project success. | A comprehensive and updated Risk Register.; Effective mitigation strategies in place.; Minimal impact from unforeseen risks.; Timely escalation of critical risks. | Ongoing (Regular risk reviews, especially at key milestones). | Risk Register (with likelihood, impact, mitigation strategies).; Contingency Plans.; Issue Logs.; Lessons Learned Documentation. | Project Leader: Leads risk identification and mitigation.; All Team Members: Identify and report risks.; Quality Assurance: Advises on quality risks.; Regulatory Affairs: Advises on regulatory risks.; Legal Counsel: Advises on legal risks. | Crucial for anticipating potential scientific failures, safety concerns, or regulatory hurdles based on published data from similar projects or therapeutic areas. Helps in developing proactive mitigation strategies. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 6: Stakeholder Communication & Reporting | To effectively communicate project status, progress, challenges, and key decisions to all relevant internal and external stakeholders. | Clear, concise, and timely project reports.; Engaged and informed stakeholders.; Effective management of stakeholder expectations.; Positive relationships with key internal and external partners. | Ongoing (Weekly/bi-weekly team updates, monthly/quarterly steering committee meetings). | Project Status Reports (e.g., traffic light reports).; Steering Committee Presentations.; Executive Summaries.; Communication Logs.; Data Presentations. | Project Leader: Primary communicator for the project.; Senior Management/Steering Committee: Receives updates, makes decisions.; Functional Heads: Receive updates relevant to their departments.; External Collaborators: Receive updates on joint projects. | Essential for presenting scientific progress, clinical data, and technical findings to diverse audiences, often requiring the ability to summarize complex medical literature clearly and concisely. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 7: Regulatory & Quality Compliance | To ensure all project activities adhere to relevant regulatory guidelines (e.g., GLP, GCP, GMP) and internal quality standards. | Project activities compliant with all applicable regulations.; Successful internal and external audits.; No significant compliance deviations.; Robust documentation of all processes and results. | Ongoing throughout project lifecycle. | Compliance Checklists.; Audit Reports.; Standard Operating Procedures (SOPs).; Training Records.; Documentation Management System. | Project Leader: Ensures compliance within the project.; Quality Assurance: Provides guidance, conducts audits.; Regulatory Affairs: Advises on regulatory requirements.; All Team Members: Adhere to SOPs and regulations. | Informs the adherence to guidelines for pre-clinical studies (GLP), clinical trials (GCP), and manufacturing (GMP), ensuring that all data generated is robust and acceptable for regulatory submissions. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 8: Problem Solving & Decision Making | To identify issues, analyze root causes, and make timely, informed decisions to keep the project on track and resolve challenges effectively. | Timely resolution of project issues.; Data-driven decision-making.; Effective escalation of critical problems.; Minimal re-work due to poor decisions. | Ongoing. | Issue Resolution Logs.; Decision Records.; Root Cause Analysis Reports.; Corrective and Preventive Actions (CAPAs). | Project Leader: Leads problem-solving, makes decisions.; Project Team: Identifies issues, contributes to solutions.; Senior Management: Approves major decisions or provides guidance for complex issues.; External Experts: May be consulted for specialized problems. | Informs problem-solving by providing precedents, alternative approaches, and scientific context from published research or clinical case studies. Helps in evaluating potential solutions. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Step 9: Project Closure & Lessons Learned | To formally close the project, ensure all deliverables are met, and capture lessons learned to improve future R&D projects. | All project deliverables completed and documented.; Formal project closure sign-off.; Comprehensive Lessons Learned Report.; Knowledge transfer to relevant teams. | 2-4 weeks (at project completion). | Project Closure Report.; Final Project Documentation Package.; Lessons Learned Workshop Summary.; Archiving of Project Data. | Project Leader: Manages project closure, facilitates lessons learned.; Project Team: Contributes to lessons learned.; Quality Assurance: Ensures documentation completeness.; R&D Management: Reviews lessons learned for organizational improvement. | Helps in understanding the broader implications of project findings, identifying areas where scientific knowledge or methodologies could be improved for future research, and contributing to the collective knowledge base. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
